      "content after edit": [
        "Here, the equation that calculates the current time-step's c_t from the previous time-step's cell state vector c_{t-1} can be understood from a perspective similar to the left-side network shown earlier.\n\nFirst, the vector corresponding to the tanh output you saw previously appears here. This is the last of the four vectors obtained by applying the tanh function. Also, this vector is element-wise multiplied by the unified-dimension vector obtained through the input gate, where each element of the vector has a value between 0 and 1. Additionally, the vector c_{t-1} that comes from the previous time-step is element-wise multiplied by another vector obtained through the forget gate, which uses the sigmoid function to produce values between 0 and 1 per dimension, controlling the previous cell state accordingly.\n\nTo summarize again, we apply the forget gate by multiplying the previous time-step's cell state vector c_{t-1} element-wise with weights between 0 and 1, selectively forgetting information from the past.\n\nThen we compute a vector representing new information derived from the current input x_t and previous hidden state h_{t-1}, again weighting each dimension between 0 and 1 to control the amount of new information added. Adding this to the previous result produces the new cell state c_t."

      "content after edit": [
        "Here, the equation that calculates the current time-step's c_t from the previous time-step's cell state vector c_{t-1} can be understood from a perspective similar to the left-side network shown earlier.\n\nFirst, the vector corresponding to the tanh output you saw previously appears here. This is the last of the four vectors obtained by applying the tanh function. Also, this vector is element-wise multiplied by the unified-dimension vector obtained through the input gate, where each element of the vector has a value between 0 and 1. Additionally, the vector c_{t-1} that comes from the previous time-step is element-wise multiplied by another vector obtained through the forget gate, which uses the sigmoid function to produce values between 0 and 1 per dimension, controlling the previous cell state accordingly.\n\nTo summarize again, we apply the forget gate by multiplying the previous time-step's cell state vector c_{t-1} element-wise with weights between 0 and 1, selectively forgetting information from the past.\n\nThen we compute a vector representing new information derived from the current input x_t and previous hidden state h_{t-1}, again weighting each dimension between 0 and 1 to control the amount of new information added. Adding this to the previous result produces the new cell state c_t."
